# Zero Net Export Bug Tracker

This document is the single source of truth for active bugs, regressions, validation status, and bug closure in this project.

If another project document appears to disagree about whether a bug is still open, whether it was validated, or whether it is actually closed, follow this file.

## How to use this file

Use this file for all of the following:
- logging a newly discovered bug or regression
- recording how the bug shows up in the real product
- tracking whether the bug is only in the repo, only in the live install, or both
- recording the fix commit or release candidate that should contain the fix
- tracking validation status
- closing the bug only after the right evidence exists

This file is for real bug state, not vague ideas.

## Bug workflow

### 1. Post a bug
When a new bug is discovered, add an entry with:
- bug id
- title
- status
- severity
- area
- where seen
- current observed behavior
- expected behavior
- evidence
- suspected cause if known
- next action

### 2. Work a bug
While fixing a bug, keep the entry updated with:
- current owner/workstream if helpful
- relevant branch/commit
- what changed
- whether the bug is believed fixed only in repo or also validated live

### 3. Validate a bug
A bug is not considered truly fixed just because code changed.
Validation should state:
- where validation happened
- what exact evidence was checked
- what version/build/commit was involved
- whether the bug is resolved in live Home Assistant or only in repo state

### 4. Close a bug
Only close a bug when the fix has the right evidence for that bug.
If the bug affects live Home Assistant behavior, closure should normally require live validation, not just repo confidence.

## Status values

Use these values:
- `open` - bug is confirmed and not yet fixed
- `in_progress` - active fix work is underway
- `fixed_pending_validation` - a fix exists in repo or candidate build, but closure evidence is still missing
- `validated` - fix has been validated with the right evidence
- `closed` - bug is complete and can be treated as done
- `deferred` - known but intentionally not the current priority

## Severity values

Use these values:
- `critical` - blocks load, setup, or the core product path
- `high` - major user-visible breakage or strong regression
- `medium` - important but not fully blocking
- `low` - minor issue, cleanup, or polish-level defect

## Bug areas

Suggested area labels:
- `runtime`
- `config_flow`
- `managed_devices`
- `source_mapping`
- `controls`
- `sensors`
- `diagnostics`
- `release`
- `docs`
- `process`

## Current active bugs

## ZNE-001 - Repairs platform contract breaks integration recovery
- **status:** `validated`
- **severity:** `critical`
- **area:** `runtime`
- **where seen:** live Home Assistant after `0.1.82` deploy/restart
- **current observed behavior:** Zero Net Export entities restore as unavailable, and logs show `HomeAssistantError: Invalid repairs platform <module 'custom_components.zero_net_export.repairs' ...>`
- **expected behavior:** Repairs platform loads cleanly and the integration recovers with live entities instead of staying restored/unavailable
- **evidence:** live HA logs after the `0.1.82` restart; affected entities included `sensor.zero_net_export_status`, `sensor.zero_net_export_command_center_status`, `sensor.zero_net_export_stale_source_count`, `binary_sensor.zero_net_export_safe_mode`, and `sensor.zero_net_export_reason`
- **suspected cause:** missing Repairs flow contract in `custom_components/zero_net_export/repairs.py`
- **repo fix:** `ad44fc1` - `fix: add repairs platform entry flow`
- **validation status:** validated against the live `0.1.83` deploy on 2026-04-15. Fresh post-restart log review no longer showed `Invalid repairs platform`, and the earlier `build_release_info()` setup-retry traceback also did not reappear. This clears the original hard-load failure even though broader entity recovery is still unresolved.
- **next action:** keep ZNE-002 open as the follow-on runtime recovery bug, because the hard repairs-platform failure is gone but the integration/entities still are not fully present live

## ZNE-002 - Main Zero Net Export entities stay restored/unavailable after restart
- **status:** `fixed_pending_validation`
- **severity:** `critical`
- **area:** `runtime`
- **where seen:** live Home Assistant after the `0.1.82` deploy/restart, and still unresolved after the exact `0.1.83` repo build was deployed to Home Assistant
- **current observed behavior:** earlier live inspection showed no active `zero_net_export` config entry and no controller device/entities after restart. That exact condition is still not present in the current live install: the config entry exists again and core Zero Net Export entities are live through the API, but another explicit restart/reload proof is still missing, so restart persistence is not yet re-validated.
- **expected behavior:** the live Home Assistant install should retain or recreate an active `zero_net_export` config entry so the controller device and core runtime entities load normally after restart
- **evidence:** earlier live SSH/API inspection showed `0` `zero_net_export` config entries, `0` Zero Net Export devices, and only `update.zero_net_export_update` visible. In this run, documented HA SSH access on `root@192.168.86.200:2222` succeeded again and direct inspection of `/config/.storage/core.config_entries` still shows one `zero_net_export` entry (`01KP8MW539MQ724BBFZX2EF6S2`, title `Zero Net Export`, created `2026-04-15T13:21:46.601855+00:00`). Direct Home Assistant API inspection in this run also returns 145 live `zero_net_export` entities, including `sensor.zero_net_export_status`, `sensor.zero_net_export_command_center_status`, `sensor.zero_net_export_unmanaged_candidate_overview`, and `button.zero_net_export_show_fleet_console`.
- **suspected cause:** the earlier missing-config-entry state was real, but the live system has since recovered past that blocker, likely via successful Add Integration. The remaining runtime/configure failures are now narrower follow-on bugs rather than absence of the entry itself.
- **validation status:** improved materially but not yet closed. The exact missing-config-entry condition is no longer reproducible live and the entity surface is back, but restart persistence still needs re-validation before this bug can be closed confidently.
- **next action:** keep this bug at `fixed_pending_validation`, then re-test restart/reload persistence after the current exact-build drift is cleared so the entry/device/entity set is proven stable across another live restart

## ZNE-003 - Requested native UI outcome still not visibly delivered
- **status:** `fixed_pending_validation`
- **severity:** `high`
- **area:** `managed_devices`
- **where seen:** product-level review against live/native UI expectations
- **current observed behavior:** repo-side Workstreams A/B have continued to tighten the native command-center and Managed Devices story, but this run still did not find a new concrete repo-side A-D/F defect stronger than the already-known release-line drift. The documented HA SSH path still works, and `python3 scripts/validate_install_fingerprint.py --ssh-host root@192.168.86.200 --ssh-port 2222 /config` still reports the same six-file exact-build mismatch on `button.py`, `config_flow.py`, `native_support.py`, `sensor.py`, `strings.json`, and `translations/en.json`, with repo and live `manifest_version` both still at `0.1.86`. The stronger drift this run is loop behavior in recent repo history: after the earlier empty-fleet wording churn (`26d12c1`, `fce766b`, `62dc6f0`, `e221549`), the latest component-changing commits `1c11775`, `049e82e`, `09bc6d4`, and `f03d606` kept spending the same still-undeployed candidate on more empty-state/review-path copy follow-ons, while nearby doc-only churn (`64da673` -> `4025b31`) repeated the same unchanged mismatch bookkeeping. That means the loop has shifted from finding one fresh product defect to reworking the same wording on an unreleased `0.1.86` build.
- **expected behavior:** the product visibly delivers:
  1. clear managed vs unmanaged device experience
  2. clear promote / vet / review flow
  3. clear separation of Controls / Sensors / Managed Devices / Diagnostics
- **evidence:** repo/design audit against `docs/UI_DESIGN.md` and `docs/UI_IMPLEMENTATION_MAP.md`, plus current repo inspection on `4e4a2b8`, `350a379`, `cbfee38`, and later `HEAD`. `rg -n "deeper managed-device review|detailed_management_summary|Use \{INTEGRATION_DEVICE_PATH\} for deeper managed-device review" custom_components/zero_net_export/config_flow.py tests` showed the remaining fallback wording leak in `ZeroNetExportOptionsFlow._detailed_management_summary()`: if the shared command-center summary ever omitted `detailed_management_summary`, the Managed Devices flow would fall back to the generic integration device page instead of the explicit secondary review path the UI map calls for. This run fixes that fallback to use `DETAILED_MANAGEMENT_PATH` and adds a focused regression in `tests/test_config_flow_device_runtime_overlay.py` so the fallback stays aligned with the documented device-page review path. A follow-on repo grep for `diagnostics/support surfaces request them` also found one remaining bucket-name leak in `custom_components/zero_net_export/release_info.py` and its regression fixtures, which was still blending Diagnostics with the retired support wording even after the rest of the four-bucket cleanup. This watchdog run then found the same retired `runtime/support` and `diagnostics/support` blend still sitting inside `docs/UI_DESIGN.md` itself under the implementation gap analysis, which meant the source-of-truth design doc was lagging the repo's four-bucket cleanup and could still mislead later audits. In this run, a long command-center fleet-state audit showed `_build_command_center_fleet_activity_summary(...)` could still exceed Home Assistant's 255-character state limit even after its first compaction pass, which made `_truncate_state_summary(..., fallback=device_status)` drop the opening operator console back to the weaker generic device-status line and lose the managed/unmanaged split the UI map expects. This run fixes that by adding a second-stage minimal fleet-activity compaction path in `custom_components/zero_net_export/native_support.py` plus a focused regression in `tests/test_command_center_summary.py` that locks the managed/unmanaged, blocked, and review-first signals in place under overflow. This run's repo audit then found one remaining unmanaged-backlog split inconsistency in `custom_components/zero_net_export/sensor.py`: `ZeroNetExportSensor.native_value` was still returning `build_candidate_overview_summary(...)` for `unmanaged_candidate_overview`, so the fleet-workspace sensor kept collapsing back to the older `top ...` summary instead of naming the explicit `review ...` and `ready ...` candidate split now shown in Configure and the device-page review path. The new `_unmanaged_candidate_overview_state(...)` helper fixes that sensor state and `tests/test_sensor_entity_categories.py` now locks the review-first plus ready-next wording into the sensor surface. This run's repo audit found the same split still missing in one part of Workstream A: `build_native_command_center_summary(...)` was deriving `review_candidate` and `ready_candidate`, but `_build_command_center_fleet_activity_summary(...)` and `_command_center_device_status_with_unmanaged_context(...)` still emitted only `review ...` and `top ...`, so the opening operator console hid the first `ready ...` candidate whenever the top unmanaged candidate also needed review. `custom_components/zero_net_export/native_support.py` now carries that `ready ...` candidate through both summaries, and `tests/test_command_center_summary.py` locks the command-center `Fleet activity` and unmanaged-context fallback to the same review-first/ready-next backlog story already used in Configure and the fleet workspace. This run then found a remaining Workstream B/D drift in the same opening command center: `build_native_setup_recommendation(...)` and `build_native_command_center_summary(...)` could still recommend Controls and generic validation wording even while managed devices needed attention or unmanaged candidates were waiting below. The repo fix now keeps the recommended section and next-step handoff anchored to Managed Devices whenever fleet follow-up still exists, with focused regressions in `tests/test_source_repair_guidance.py` and `tests/test_command_center_summary.py`. This run found one more Managed Devices workspace gap after that opening-console cleanup: `sensor.zero_net_export_managed_fleet_overview` still omitted the ready-to-promote backlog count even though `docs/UI_IMPLEMENTATION_MAP.md` explicitly says that count should stay visible at a glance. The repo fix keeps that `1 ready to promote` / `N ready to promote` signal in the managed-fleet workspace state string, preserves it under summary compaction by dropping lower-value `enabled` / `usable` fragments before truncating the core backlog story, and adds focused coverage in `tests/test_sensor_entity_categories.py` for both the new state text and the exported `review_candidate` / `ready_candidate` attributes. This run's repo audit found one more Workstream D/F polish gap in the Sensors path itself: the native source-mapping step was still titled `Source mapping` and led with a long duplicated selector-fallback paragraph, which kept the Sensors bucket less legible than the rest of the four-bucket flow. The repo fix renames that step to `Sensors`, trims the opening copy, and keeps the fallback guidance in its own blocker-only section with focused regression coverage in `tests/test_bucket_ownership_copy.py`. This run then found one more Workstream B/C follow-on in `custom_components/zero_net_export/strings.json`: the promotion, edit, remove, and enablement Configure steps were carrying snapshots but not the explicit `Managed Devices: {device_count}` / `Unmanaged candidate devices: {candidate_count}` totals consistently, so operators could lose backlog scale while moving through the native promotion path. The repo fix restores those totals across the managed-device follow-on screens and keeps translation sync exact. This run found the next adjacent Workstream B/C follow-on in the same area: those follow-on screens still assembled managed/unmanaged workspace placeholders independently, so the richer fixed-load and variable-load surfaced-candidate summaries were not locked to travel with the rest of the Managed Devices workspace context. `custom_components/zero_net_export/config_flow.py` now centralizes those workspace placeholders in `_managed_devices_workspace_placeholders(...)`, extends them with per-kind candidate summary blocks, and reuses that shared context across shortlist, full-list, review, preset, save, bulk-enable, edit, and remove screens. `tests/test_bucket_ownership_copy.py` and `tests/test_config_flow_device_runtime_overlay.py` now lock both the new copy placeholders and their runtime values into the promotion follow-on path. This run found one more Workstream B follow-on in the exact same managed-fleet surface: `_overlay_runtime_device_details(...)` was already receiving runtime-duration telemetry for managed devices, but `ZeroNetExportOptionsFlow._device_status_label(...)` was dropping it, so Configure -> Managed Devices could still feel flatter than the deeper device-page review even when Home Assistant had current-runtime data. The repo fix now carries `current_active_seconds` and `active_runtime_today_seconds` through the overlay and surfaces compact `runtime ...` / `today ...` fragments directly in the managed-device rows so the top workspace reads more like an active fleet console instead of a static inventory list. This run found one more Workstream A weak spot in the opening operator console: long `Fleet activity` strings could still crowd out the managed/unmanaged story, especially when a managed device needed attention and the unmanaged backlog had both review-first and ready-next candidates. `custom_components/zero_net_export/native_support.py` now keeps `attention first`, blocked/planned managed signals, and the `review ...` / `ready ...` backlog split visible through additional compaction tiers instead of collapsing back to a weaker generic fallback. This run found the next adjacent Workstream A overflow case after that: very large fixed and variable candidate-mix counts could still consume the remaining 255-character budget before the more important `review ...` and `ready ...` cues, even though those cues are what the opening operator console needs to preserve first. The current repo fix now drops oversized fixed/variable candidate-count mix fragments and low-value planned-action counts ahead of the review-first and ready-next backlog story when those large count labels would otherwise crowd out the key operator signals, and `tests/test_command_center_summary.py` locks that compaction ordering in place. This run then found one more Workstream A/B handoff gap in the same command-center strip: when every unmanaged candidate was already promotion-ready, `build_native_command_center_summary(...)` still built no unmanaged alert at all, so the top alert strip could hide the ready-only backlog even while `Fleet activity` below showed `N ready to promote`. The repo fix now emits `Unmanaged ready next: ...` in that ready-only case and adds a focused regression in `tests/test_command_center_summary.py` so the opening operator console keeps the same ready-next fleet story as Managed Devices.
- **suspected cause:** the bug tracker had accumulated resolved sub-findings faster than the current entry was being pruned, so the source-of-truth bug state started lagging behind the shipped repo candidate and the implementation map's workstream ordering.
- **repo fix:** earlier repo fixes remain listed above. This run closes one more Workstream B operator-console drift: `custom_components/zero_net_export/config_flow.py` and `custom_components/zero_net_export/sensor.py` now keep active-runtime cues visible when the same managed load is also the current attention-first or planned item, so Configure fleet summaries and the primary device-page managed summary no longer flatten that row back to a non-running attention/plan label. Focused regressions in `tests/test_config_flow_device_runtime_overlay.py` and `tests/test_sensor_entity_categories.py` lock that active-with-attention/planned wording in place. This run also closes one more matching Controls follow-through leak in `custom_components/zero_net_export/config_flow.py`: the empty-fleet Controls step now reuses the same review-first plus ready-next Managed Devices handoff already shown elsewhere when surfaced unmanaged candidates exist, instead of falling straight back to manual-add wording and hiding the current promotion path. `tests/test_config_flow_device_runtime_overlay.py` now locks that regression. This run closes the matching config-flow follow-through leak in `custom_components/zero_net_export/config_flow.py`: the Sensors `source_next_step` handoff and the Managed Devices `device_next_step` summary now keep the first ready-next candidate visible whenever a different unmanaged candidate still needs review first, instead of dropping back to a review-only sentence and hiding the next promotion target already shown elsewhere in the product. This run also tightens the opening command-center copy in `custom_components/zero_net_export/strings.json` and `custom_components/zero_net_export/translations/en.json` so it no longer tells operators to defer Managed Devices categorically until blockers clear, and instead says `When the next step moves into fleet work, continue in Managed Devices.` `tests/test_config_flow_device_runtime_overlay.py` now locks both follow-through paths to that review-first plus ready-next story. This run adds one opening-console follow-on in `custom_components/zero_net_export/native_support.py` so `Fleet activity` can name the split backlog mix directly as `fixed backlog ...` and `variable backlog ...` when fixed and variable unmanaged candidates diverge between review-first and ready-next states, instead of only showing the aggregate review/ready totals plus a single candidate preview. Focused regression coverage in `tests/test_command_center_summary.py` now locks that per-kind backlog wording in place while also proving the overflow compaction path still drops those extra mix fragments before the higher-value `review ...` / `ready ...` cues when the 255-character Home Assistant state limit gets tight. This run extends that same managed/unmanaged backlog mix into the command-center `device_status` fallback path, so the opening operator console keeps the fixed-versus-variable review/ready split visible even when Home Assistant or other native surfaces fall back to the shorter device-status line instead of the full `Fleet activity` state. This run mirrors that backlog-mix story into `custom_components/zero_net_export/sensor.py`, so the Managed Devices workspace sensors now surface `fixed backlog ...` and `variable backlog ...` alongside the existing review-first and ready-next cues, and focused regressions in `tests/test_sensor_entity_categories.py` lock the per-kind backlog wording plus exported fixed/variable review-ready counts into both the managed-fleet and unmanaged-candidate overview sensors. This run also fixes one remaining cross-bucket follow-through leak in `custom_components/zero_net_export/config_flow.py`: the healthy Controls screen had still been overriding a command-center `Managed Devices` recommendation with a generic `verify the current controller outcome` step, which could steer operators away from pending fleet attention or promotion work even though Workstreams B/C were still the mapped next gap. The policy step now reuses the command-center `next_action_summary` whenever Managed Devices still owns the real follow-through, and `tests/test_config_flow_device_runtime_overlay.py` locks that regression. This run also removes one remaining Workstream B/D wording leak across `custom_components/zero_net_export/native_support.py`, `custom_components/zero_net_export/sensor.py`, and `custom_components/zero_net_export/config_flow.py`: unmanaged-candidate handoffs now explicitly tell operators to review the `Managed Devices workspace`, starting in the unmanaged section, instead of falling back to the older generic `review first in the unmanaged section` phrasing. `tests/test_command_center_summary.py`, `tests/test_sensor_entity_categories.py`, and `tests/test_config_flow_device_runtime_overlay.py` now lock that workspace-first wording into the opening command center, fleet helper sensor, and managed-device follow-through copy. This run also keeps that richer backlog story visible inside the Managed Devices config-flow snapshot itself: `custom_components/zero_net_export/config_flow.py` now adds `fixed backlog ...` and `variable backlog ...` fragments to `_unmanaged_snapshot_text(...)` whenever review-first and ready-next candidates split by kind, and `tests/test_config_flow_device_runtime_overlay.py` locks both the mixed fixed/variable case and the single-kind fixed backlog wording in place. This run closes one smaller follow-on in the same success landing: `_post_save_candidate_follow_through(...)` now keeps the save handoff explicitly tied to the Managed Devices workspace instead of the older generic review-first phrasing, and `tests/test_config_flow_device_runtime_overlay.py` locks the promotion and removal notifications to that follow-through copy. This run also normalizes the remaining ready-only unmanaged promotion handoffs across `custom_components/zero_net_export/native_support.py`, `custom_components/zero_net_export/sensor.py`, and `custom_components/zero_net_export/config_flow.py` so they now read `review the Managed Devices workspace, then promote next from the unmanaged section ...` instead of the clumsier mixed `...and promote...` / repeated-section wording. Focused regressions in `tests/test_command_center_summary.py`, `tests/test_sensor_entity_categories.py`, and `tests/test_config_flow_device_runtime_overlay.py` lock that more natural ready-next phrasing into the command-center, fleet helper sensor, and Configure follow-through surfaces. This run adds one more Workstream B follow-on in `custom_components/zero_net_export/config_flow.py` and `custom_components/zero_net_export/sensor.py`: when the managed fleet is healthy but actively running, the Managed Devices snapshot now names the first active device directly instead of stopping at aggregate active-load counts, so the top of the workspace reads more like a live fleet console than a passive inventory summary. `tests/test_config_flow_device_runtime_overlay.py` and `tests/test_sensor_entity_categories.py` now lock that active-device snapshot detail into both the Configure workspace copy and the managed-fleet overview sensor. This run closes the matching opening-console follow-on in `custom_components/zero_net_export/native_support.py`: `Fleet activity` now names the first active managed device directly in healthy runtime states, so Configure's top-board managed snapshot no longer lags behind the richer active-device detail already shown in Managed Devices. `tests/test_command_center_summary.py` now locks that `active device ...` detail into the command-center summary too. This run adds the same backlog-mix story to the `managed_fleet_ready` sensor, so the Managed Devices helper surface now keeps `fixed backlog ...` and `variable backlog ...` visible before the existing ready-next and review-first candidate cues, with focused regressions covering both mixed fixed/variable and fixed-only backlogs. This run closes one more Managed Devices workspace follow-on in `custom_components/zero_net_export/config_flow.py`: the top `Fleet summary` line now carries the same `attention first ...`, `blocked ...`, `plan ...`, and healthy `active device ...` focus labels already present in the compact managed snapshot, so the primary fleet workspace reads like a live operator console even before an operator scans the per-device rows. `tests/test_config_flow_device_runtime_overlay.py` now locks those richer managed-summary cues into the main Managed Devices flow and its promotion follow-on screens. This run moves that same top-line summary one step closer to a screenshot-grade fleet console by reordering the `Fleet summary` itself around attention, blocked/planned activity, and active runtime before the lower-value inventory counts, so the first line of Configure -> Managed Devices now leads with the current operational story instead of burying it behind generic enabled/usable totals. `tests/test_config_flow_device_runtime_overlay.py` now locks that higher-signal ordering into the managed-device workspace. This run closes a remaining Workstream B handoff gap in the same Managed Devices flow: `_device_next_step(...)` now preserves the command-center's blocked-managed and attention-first fleet guidance when Managed Devices already owns the next step, instead of dropping back to unmanaged promotion copy whenever surfaced candidates also exist. Focused regressions in `tests/test_config_flow_device_runtime_overlay.py` now lock both the blocked-managed and managed-attention handoffs into the Configure workspace follow-through. This run also tightens the promotion flow wording in `custom_components/zero_net_export/strings.json`, `custom_components/zero_net_export/translations/en.json`, and `custom_components/zero_net_export/button.py` so shortlist, full-list, review, preset, and handoff copy read as one explicit promotion workflow instead of a stack of generic picker labels. This run adds one more Workstream A/B fleet-legibility fix across `custom_components/zero_net_export/config_flow.py`, `custom_components/zero_net_export/native_support.py`, and `custom_components/zero_net_export/sensor.py`: when one managed device needs attention or has the next planned action but a different managed device is the active runtime load, the native summaries now keep that distinct `active device ...` row visible instead of hiding it whenever any attention/planned state exists anywhere in the fleet. Focused regressions in `tests/test_config_flow_device_runtime_overlay.py`, `tests/test_command_center_summary.py`, and `tests/test_sensor_entity_categories.py` now lock that split attention-versus-active runtime story into Configure, Fleet activity, and the managed-fleet overview sensor. This run also closes one remaining Workstream D wording leak in `custom_components/zero_net_export/strings.json` and `custom_components/zero_net_export/translations/en.json`: the Controls intro no longer says Controls owns controller behaviour only once source mapping and managed devices are already healthy, and instead keeps Controls bucket-first by saying it owns controller behaviour and outcome while Sensors, Managed Devices, and Diagnostics keep their own jobs. `tests/test_bucket_ownership_copy.py` now locks that wording in place. This run also tightens the last weaker managed-device handoff phrasing across `custom_components/zero_net_export/native_support.py`, `custom_components/zero_net_export/sensor.py`, `custom_components/zero_net_export/config_flow.py`, and `custom_components/zero_net_export/button.py`: attention-first fleet follow-through now says `review the Managed Devices workspace, starting with attention on ...`, and empty-fleet no-candidate follow-through now keeps the same workspace-first story by telling operators to review Managed Devices before adding the first fixed or variable load manually. W` runtime signal visible instead of collapsing back to a flatter kind-only label. `tests/test_command_center_summary.py` now locks that active-runtime cue into the top board while the separate `plan ...` row still carries the action detail. ## ZNE-005 - `build_release_info()` missing required `current_version` argument
- **status:** `validated`
- **severity:** `critical`
- **area:** `runtime`
- **where seen:** live Home Assistant integration page during setup/retry
- **current observed behavior:** historical bug. Earlier live Home Assistant runs showed `Failed setup, will retry: build_release_info() missing 1 required positional argument: 'current_version'`.
- **expected behavior:** Zero Net Export setup should complete without this runtime error
- **evidence:** user screenshot of the Home Assistant integration page showing the exact setup error; repo/HA SSH inspection on 2026-04-15 confirmed the live `0.1.81` install still had `coordinator.py` calling `build_release_info(include_changelog=False)` at line 223 without the required version argument. In this run, documented HA SSH/API access confirmed the live install now has one active `zero_net_export` config entry and 145 live Zero Net Export entities, `scripts/validate_install_fingerprint.py` shows `coordinator.py` matches the repo candidate exactly, and fresh `ha core logs` review no longer shows the earlier `build_release_info()` missing-argument retry.
- **suspected cause:** coordinator release-update metadata called `build_release_info()` without the required `current_version`, causing setup to fail while building validation details
- **repo fix:** `48a9d45` - pass `INTEGRATION_VERSION` from `coordinator.py` into `build_release_info()` and cover the call contract with a coordinator unit test; this run adds `tests/test_release_update_details.py` so the release-update path has its own focused regression coverage for the missing-argument contract
- **validation status:** repo-side fix remains covered by `python3 -m unittest tests.test_source_freshness_probes tests.test_release_info_install_guidance tests.test_release_update_details` plus `python3 -m py_compile custom_components/zero_net_export/coordinator.py`. Live validation is now good enough for this bug specifically: the fixed `coordinator.py` is present in the live install, the integration has an active config entry again, and the earlier missing-argument setup retry is no longer present in current log review.
- **next action:** no further action for this specific bug beyond keeping future coordinator/release-info changes under regression coverage

## ZNE-029 - Fleet workspace candidate sensors redo full candidate discovery on every sensor read
- **status:** `fixed_pending_validation`
- **severity:** `medium`
- **area:** `sensors`
- **where seen:** live Home Assistant logs on the current mixed `0.1.86` install
- **current observed behavior:** Home Assistant logged `Updating state for sensor.zero_net_export_unmanaged_candidate_overview ... took 0.593 seconds`, which means the main Managed Devices candidate surface is still heavy enough to trigger runtime warnings in the live install.
- **expected behavior:** the fleet workspace candidate sensors should reuse one candidate-discovery result per coordinator refresh instead of rescanning the entire HA state registry separately for each related sensor value.
- **evidence:** this run used the documented SSH path in `TOOLS.md` and `ha core logs -n 400 | grep -i "entity.py\|blocking call\|zero_net_export"`, which returned `2026-04-16 17:10:11.612 WARNING ... sensor.zero_net_export_unmanaged_candidate_overview ... took 0.593 seconds`; this run's repo inspection then confirmed `custom_components/zero_net_export/sensor.py` was calling `discover_candidate_devices(...)` independently for `managed_fleet_overview`, `unmanaged_candidate_count`, `unmanaged_candidate_overview`, `top_unmanaged_candidate`, `top_candidate_fit`, `top_candidate_warnings`, `candidate_shortlist`, `candidate_shortlist_fit`, and `fleet_console_next_step`, all against the same coordinator state. This watchdog run found one more repo-side rediscovery leak in the same area: those fleet-workspace sensors were now caching candidate discovery for their main state values, but their `extra_state_attributes` path was still calling `_candidate_devices_for_hass(...)` directly and re-scanning Home Assistant state again instead of reusing the same per-refresh cache.
- **suspected cause:** fleet workspace sensors were each re-running full candidate discovery from `hass.states.async_all()` during the same coordinator update instead of sharing one cached candidate list, and the first repo-side caching pass only covered `native_value` while leaving `extra_state_attributes` on the old direct rediscovery path.
- **repo fix:** `c380a77` cached fleet candidate discovery per coordinator snapshot in `custom_components/zero_net_export/sensor.py`, and `3cb05a0` extends that same fix so the fleet-workspace sensors' `extra_state_attributes` now reuse `_candidate_devices_for_state(...)` instead of triggering a second full discovery pass. `tests/test_sensor_entity_categories.py` now also locks that regression by asserting the managed-fleet overview state plus attributes share one candidate-discovery call per coordinator snapshot.
- **validation status:** repo-side fix verified again in this run with `python3 -m unittest tests.test_sensor_entity_categories -q` and `python3 -m unittest discover -s tests -q`. Live validation is still pending because the optimized sensor code is not yet installed on the live Home Assistant build.
- **next action:** deploy one exact current repo build, rerun fingerprint validation until `overall_match=true`, then confirm the unmanaged-candidate sensors stop emitting slow-update warnings in Home Assistant logs

## ZNE-026 - Integration overview/device page still shows stale version, and the first repo-side fix regressed into blocking I/O
- **status:** `fixed_pending_validation`
- **severity:** `high`
- **area:** `release`
- **where seen:** live Home Assistant UI after `0.1.84`, and again during `0.1.85` live validation
- **current observed behavior:** version fidelity on the HA integration/device surfaces was unstable. Earlier screenshots showed `Version 0.1.83` / `Firmware: 0.1.83` after a `0.1.84` deploy, and the first repo-side fix for this then triggered Home Assistant blocking-I/O warnings from `entity.py` while reading `manifest.json` on the event loop during setup.
- **expected behavior:** the Home Assistant integration and device surfaces should show the currently installed package version without introducing new blocking-call warnings during startup
- **evidence:** user screenshots on 2026-04-16 showed the integration header and device info card rendering `0.1.83` after the `0.1.84` release/deploy. In the last live validation, post-restart HA logs showed `Detected blocking call to read_text ... at custom_components/zero_net_export/entity.py, line 16` and `Detected blocking call to open ...` from `_device_surface_version()`, which had been introduced to fix the stale-version display. Repo inspection in the fix run confirmed `custom_components/zero_net_export/entity.py` was still doing that synchronous manifest read for every entity device-info build. A later repo-wide fingerprint rerun widened the currently shipped drift set beyond this single file, but the documented HA SSH path still shows the same live `entity.py` warning at `2026-04-16 10:03`, and the fingerprint output still includes the older live `entity.py` hash (`2dffb9a4ef0c` remote vs `9b087d27adff` repo) among the remaining mismatches.
- **suspected cause:** the original stale version was partly a real live mixed-build problem, but the repo-side fix duplicated manifest reading inside entity initialization instead of reusing the already-derived packaged integration version, which violates HA async expectations and is not safe to ship as the final solution.
- **repo fix:** this run removes the synchronous `_device_surface_version()` manifest read from `custom_components/zero_net_export/entity.py` and feeds the native device surface directly from `INTEGRATION_VERSION`, which already tracks the packaged component version. `tests/test_device_surface_version.py` now verifies the device surface uses the integration version constant without depending on manifest I/O during entity setup.
- **validation status:** repo-side fix remains verified with `python3 -m unittest tests.test_device_surface_version -q` plus `python3 -m unittest discover -s tests -q`, which passed again in this run. Live Home Assistant validation is still pending because the currently installed fingerprint still includes the older `entity.py` and the old blocking-I/O warning remains visible until the exact current repo candidate is redeployed.
- **next action:** redeploy the exact current repo candidate, rerun fingerprint validation until `overall_match=true`, then confirm the integration/device surfaces still show the installed package version while Home Assistant startup logs no longer emit the `entity.py` blocking-I/O warning

## ZNE-027 - Command center still lets diagnostics/release plumbing dominate the primary operator surface
- **status:** `fixed_pending_validation`
- **severity:** `high`
- **area:** `diagnostics`
- **where seen:** live Home Assistant command-center modal after `0.1.84` deploy
- **current observed behavior:** the live `0.1.84` command-center modal still shows dense release-fingerprint/install-validation/debug text and long repair-path prose high in the modal, so diagnostics/support detail is visually carrying too much of the primary operator experience. Repo-side drift narrowed again in this run: after the earlier `native_support.py` cleanup, the Configure-side Diagnostics step in `custom_components/zero_net_export/strings.json` and `translations/en.json` was still carrying the older `Mapped-source triage` wall with duplicated source-role detail instead of the tighter blocker-first structure already used by the device-page Diagnostics guide, so one native Diagnostics path had been tightened while the other still lagged behind Workstream F. This watchdog run found the next smaller but real follow-on gap in that same device-page Diagnostics guide: the Python-built `build_native_support_center()` surface had stayed looser than the shipped Configure Diagnostics path by omitting the explicit diagnostics follow-through handoff, selector-workaround line, and exact-build next-step/install-evidence handoff, so the secondary native support path was still less consistent and less operator-ready than the Configure-side Diagnostics source of truth. This run found one more concrete secondary-surface drift in the same guide: `build_native_command_center_summary()` was not exporting `blocking_validation_details`, so the device-page Diagnostics guide could silently fall back to `Blocking validation details: None` even when Sensors still had real validation errors.
- **expected behavior:** per `docs/UI_DESIGN.md`, Configure should remain the primary operator workspace with the decision summary, grouped control board, and clear jump-off entries, while Diagnostics stays visible but secondary rather than dominating the landing surface.
- **evidence:** user screenshot on 2026-04-16 shows the modal headed `Zero Net Export command center` with install-fingerprint details and long repair-path prose before the main setup/operator sections, which matched the repo strings that embedded an `Installed package details:` block directly in the primary command-center description. Later repo work removed that diagnostics-heavy lead, but this run's repo inspection found the shared device-page `Show command center guide` builder in `custom_components/zero_net_export/native_support.py` had still drifted behind the shipped Configure wording: it kept the older `Headline` / `Top alert` prose, still showed the stale `Not here` tail section, and omitted the newer `Now` plus `Bucket ownership` structure already present in `strings.json`. That meant the Zero Net Export device-page command-center handoff was still less productized than the Configure landing even in repo state. A later repo pass fixed that guide, but this watchdog run found the matching drift still open in the Configure-side Diagnostics step itself: `rg -n "Mapped-source triage|Current blocker summary|Blocking mapped roles" custom_components/zero_net_export/strings.json custom_components/zero_net_export/translations/en.json custom_components/zero_net_export/native_support.py tests/test_bucket_ownership_copy.py` showed `native_support.py` already using `Blocker triage` while the shipped translated Diagnostics step still exposed `Mapped-source triage`. This run aligns the translated step with the same shorter blocker-first structure and updates `tests/test_bucket_ownership_copy.py` to lock the new `Current blocker summary` / `Blocking mapped roles` / `If Sensors owns the repair, use ...` copy in place. This watchdog run then traced the remaining device-page Diagnostics drift directly in `custom_components/zero_net_export/native_support.py`: `build_native_support_center()` was still missing the explicit `Diagnostics follow-through`, selector-workaround fallback line, and `Exact-build next step` / `Full install evidence` handoff already present in the Configure-side Diagnostics copy built from `config_flow.py`. Focused regression coverage in `tests/test_source_repair_guidance.py` now locks those lines into the device-page guide and explicitly rejects the older `Install provenance:` line that had been carrying too much of the support burden. This run then confirmed the follow-on validation-detail drift directly in repo state: `build_native_support_center()` was reading `command_center.get("blocking_validation_details")`, but `build_native_command_center_summary()` never returned that key, so the device-page Diagnostics guide could hide real Sensors validation errors behind a false `None`. `tests/test_source_repair_guidance.py` now locks the real blocking-validation text into the secondary Diagnostics guide.
- **suspected cause:** the options-flow copy and the shared device-page guide text were being tightened through different paths, so the Python-built command-center guide in `native_support.py` drifted behind the translated Configure copy and kept older setup/ownership wording longer than intended.
- **repo fix:** `d50a4b6` - update `custom_components/zero_net_export/native_support.py` so the shared device-page `Show command center guide` now matches the shipped setup-first operator-board hierarchy: `Now`, the grouped control board, a fuller setup check including source-map and repair-path context, and the same `Bucket ownership` section used by the Configure copy, while dropping the older `Not here` tail section. Focused regression coverage in `tests/test_command_center_setup_focus.py` and `tests/test_source_repair_guidance.py` now locks that guide text to the same setup-first structure already asserted for `strings.json` in `tests/test_command_center_modal_copy.py`. ## ZNE-028 - Device page still lacks the managed-device structure required by the UI design
- **status:** `fixed_pending_validation`
- **severity:** `high`
- **area:** `managed_devices`
- **where seen:** live Home Assistant device page after `0.1.84` deploy
- **current observed behavior:** the device page is still mostly generic cards plus buttons/sensors, with too little managed-device structure visible in the deeper native review path. The current bug is no longer that the device page fails to become the primary fleet workspace; it is that the deeper review path still does not feel rich or legible enough in support of Configure -> Managed Devices. Earlier repo work closed one audit-legibility gap by splitting the deeper `Review managed devices` output into `Managed devices needing attention first` and `Other managed devices`, so blocked, actively planned, or recently failed loads no longer sit in one undifferentiated audit list. This run closes the matching one-line snapshot gap on the same device-page review surfaces: the top `managed_snapshot` summary feeding `Review managed devices workspace`, `Review managed devices`, and per-device review context had still omitted managed-attention burden even when those same surfaces already exposed `attention_count` and attention-first row ordering below. This watchdog run found one smaller but still visible primary-workspace wording leak in the same Managed Devices path too: the Configure bulk-enable action and fallback next-step text were still telling operators to `Review fleet` even after the shipped UI had otherwise moved to explicit `Managed Devices workspace` wording. This run found the next remaining Workstream E detail gap inside the per-device `Review {device}` path: even after the top-level deeper audit view was split by attention, the per-device review still lacked explicit fleet-attention context, so operators inspecting one load could not immediately tell whether that device was in the current attention-first bucket or what other managed devices still needed review. A smaller follow-on drift remained in the same device-page review surfaces: they named the `Ready-next` unmanaged candidate and its usefulness, but still omitted the matching warning line, so the deeper native review path was not yet carrying the full shortlist-style `usefulness + key warning` cue the UI design expects. This run then found a smaller but real remaining snapshot drift on the same device-page review path: when the top unmanaged candidate needed review, the button-side unmanaged snapshot still failed to name the first `ready next` candidate, so the deeper review surface kept showing a vaguer backlog split than Configure -> Managed Devices. This run closes the matching detail-panel drift one level deeper too: `Review {device}` was still surfacing only the top unmanaged candidate plus the review-first candidate, so operators inspecting a managed load could still lose the first ready-to-promote candidate even after the broader workspace and save-feedback surfaces had been aligned. This run found one more Workstream E audit-depth gap in that same per-device review: after adding fleet-attention context, the detail view still named peer devices but did not preview any of their richer audit rows, so operators had to jump back out to `Review managed devices` to compare whether the next attention item was blocked, actively planned, or recently failing. This run closes the matching per-device attribute drift too: the `Review {device}` notification already carried `Ready-next candidate` context, but the button attributes still stopped at top/review-first unmanaged candidates, so automations and deeper native context consumers could miss the same ready-next backlog signal now shown in the notification body. This run then makes `Review {device}` read more like a true audit surface by adding a current-device audit snapshot plus explicit review-order context, so operators can immediately see the current row in the same richer audit format and know where that device sits inside the attention-first or steady bucket. This run closes one more smaller device-page promotion-copy drift too: the workspace and deeper review notifications were still listing `Top unmanaged candidates` with older state-heavy labels, so the secondary review path was lagging the shortlist-style `name + type + usefulness + key warning` preview already used elsewhere in Managed Devices.
- **expected behavior:** per `docs/UI_DESIGN.md` and `docs/UI_IMPLEMENTATION_MAP.md`, Configure -> Managed Devices should remain the primary fleet workspace, while the native device page should act as a clearly secondary but still first-class deeper review path with stronger managed-device structure, better per-device operational detail, and less generic helper-card feel.
- **evidence:** user screenshot on 2026-04-16 shows the device page still dominated by generic Controls/Sensors/Activity cards and button entities like `Show fleet console` / `Show managed-device review`, while the user explicitly stated that managed devices should be on the device info page and that the page has not really progressed enough toward the design. Earlier repo inspection confirmed the per-device surface was still exposing too many deep runtime sensors as primary entities, which diluted the managed-device workspace signal on the native device page. In a later repo pass, those secondary per-device status, guard, planned-action, and planned-delta entities had already been pushed into diagnostics, but this run's repo inspection still found the surviving primary `managed summary` row too sparse because it omitted the load kind and, for variable devices, hid target/guard pressure behind diagnostics or the deeper review button. This run also confirmed the remaining device-page action labels and diagnostics metadata were still leaning on helper-ish `fleet console` / `managed review` wording instead of the stronger Managed Devices workspace and review-first wording the native UI design calls for. Repo inspection in this run then found a follow-on device-page contradiction: the `Review managed devices workspace` notification still printed a promotion handoff even while the shared command-center recommendation was telling operators to repair Sensors/source blockers first, and the same contradiction still leaked through the companion `Review managed devices` notification, which weakened the global-plus-local blocker model right on the native device page. A later repo pass in this run also showed those same device-page review surfaces still reduced blocked and active-plan posture to anonymous counts in the top snapshot line, forcing operators to read deeper rows before they could tell which managed load currently needed attention. This watchdog run found one more top-line legibility gap in the same snapshot path: when a managed load needed attention but was not also blocked or actively planned, the one-line `managed_snapshot` still named the attention burden only as a count and omitted the first affected device. This run then found another device-page review regression in repo state: managed-device rows with an empty or missing `planned_action` were still being counted as active plans inside the workspace/review snapshot strings and button attributes, which could falsely surface `plan ...` and `planned action(s)` hints even when no plan existed. Repo inspection in this run then found the ordered device-page workspace and review lists still surfaced healthy planned loads before blocked managed devices, so the local managed-device review could bury the first exception even though the snapshot already named it. A follow-on repo pass in this run found one more device-page legibility gap: the managed-device workspace and review rows were still omitting load kind, priority, and current power, and variable-device rows still hid their current target power, so the deeper native review path was not yet showing the operational row detail the UI design expects. This run's repo inspection found one smaller but still visible detail-review leak in the same path: fixed-load `Review {device}` output was still printing variable-only `Requested target power`, `Variable range`, and `Step size` lines as `n/a`, while operator override lines still fell back to raw values instead of concise operator-facing wording. This watchdog run found the next Workstream E gap one level up in the same device-page review path: `Review managed devices` was still rendering the same compact row shape as the top workspace, so the supposed deeper audit view was not yet visibly richer than `Review managed devices workspace` even when last-action timing and nominal-load context were available in coordinator state. This run closed that next audit-row gap in repo state too by carrying each managed device's last requested power, last applied power, and success/failure run counts directly into the richer `Review managed devices` row summaries. This run then tightened the same deeper audit rows again so non-success managed-device reviews now carry a compact last-result fragment inline, keeping the device-page review path more diagnostic and audit-friendly without bloating the top workspace rows. A follow-on repo inspection in this run also confirmed those workspace, review, and per-device button surfaces were still rediscovering unmanaged candidates separately against the same coordinator snapshot until `2cc6e83` landed, so the deeper native review path was also carrying avoidable repeat discovery work. This run's repo inspection then found that even after the per-device detail gained fleet-attention context, the peer-device section still stopped at plain name lists, so the supposedly deeper audit path still hid whether the next peer device was blocked, planned, or recently failing unless operators backed out into the broader review list.
- **suspected cause:** managed-device UX on the device page remains implemented mainly as button-triggered review flows and supporting entities rather than as a clearly shaped secondary review surface aligned with the current design. The per-device entity mix was also too flat, leaving secondary runtime status/action detail to compete with the main managed-device summary instead of staying secondary, and the surviving primary summary row itself was still too skeletal to carry the deeper-review legibility burden the device page now owns. The detailed review payload was also still inheriting some generic profile fields without checking device kind, which left fixed loads showing variable-only `n/a` lines and raw operator-override values in the middle of an otherwise operator-facing review.

## ZNE-040 - Runtime attention notification is overloaded and poorly formatted
- **status:** `fixed_pending_validation`
- **severity:** `medium`
- **area:** `ui`
- **where seen:** live Home Assistant runtime attention notification/modal on 2026-04-16
- **current observed behavior:** the `Runtime attention needed` surface is a dense wall of text with weak visual hierarchy. The headings are not visually separated enough, spacing is poor, and the content is too long and repetitive, making the error harder to act on quickly.
- **expected behavior:** the runtime attention surface should use tighter content, clearer grouping, and stronger heading emphasis so the operator can scan the problem, cause, and next step quickly
- **evidence:** user screenshot on 2026-04-16 shows the runtime attention modal with long repeated validation details, weak spacing, and overloaded instructions. User explicitly requested bolded headings, better spacing, and tighter content.
- **suspected cause:** the current runtime/support notification text is generated as a long plain-text dump of support fields rather than being edited into a compact operator-facing alert format
- **repo fix:** this run tightens the Repairs/runtime-attention notification copy in `custom_components/zero_net_export/strings.json` and `custom_components/zero_net_export/translations/en.json`, replacing the long paragraph-style dump with short `Now`, `Mapped-source blockers`, `Do next`, and `Open` sections so the primary signal and repair path scan cleanly in Home Assistant's native modal. `a42b785` then splits the selector fallback out of `Do next` into its own `Fallback, only if Home Assistant rejects a valid choice` section so the repair path reads in the intended priority order.
- **validation status:** repo-side copy fix implemented and advanced again in this run. `tests/test_repairs_copy.py` now asserts the separate `Fallback` section instead of the older inline fallback bullet, and `python3 -m unittest tests.test_repairs_copy tests.test_translation_sync -q` plus `python3 -m unittest discover -s tests -q` passed. Live Home Assistant validation is still pending on the next exact-build redeploy.
- **next action:** redeploy the current repo candidate, then confirm the `Runtime attention needed` modal now reads as a compact sectioned alert instead of a wall of text

## ZNE-042 - Source-freshness fallback regressed and now crashes repo-side probe coverage
- **status:** `validated`
- **severity:** `medium`
- **area:** `runtime`
- **where seen:** repo HEAD test suite on 2026-04-17 after the latest source-label cleanup landed
- **current observed behavior:** historical repo-side regression. The crash no longer reproduces in the current repo test suite.
- **expected behavior:** source-freshness diagnostics should preserve the new friendly-name fallback without crashing when the state-like object only provides `name` and `last_updated`.
- **evidence:** the original failing coverage came from `python3 -m unittest discover -s tests -q`, which raised `AttributeError: 'types.SimpleNamespace' object has no attribute 'attributes'` from `custom_components/zero_net_export/coordinator.py` line 831 while exercising `test_stale_energy_sensor_is_visible_but_does_not_block_runtime` and `test_power_sensor_without_companion_probe_stays_stale`. In this run, the full repo suite still passes, so the repo-side crash remains resolved.
- **suspected cause:** the latest raw-source-id cleanup added `state.attributes.get("friendly_name")` directly inside `_source_freshness(...)` without guarding for the repo's state-like probe fixtures or other minimal state objects.
- **repo fix:** this run hardens `custom_components/zero_net_export/coordinator.py` to read `attributes = getattr(state, "attributes", None) or {}` before looking for `friendly_name`, so the new label fallback stays compatible with lightweight probe objects as well as real Home Assistant states.

- **next action:** no further action for this specific bug beyond keeping the freshness-probe regression coverage in place

## ZNE-011 - Backup artifacts still pollute Home Assistant module discovery
- **status:** `fixed_pending_validation`
- **severity:** `critical`
- **area:** `config_flow`
- **where seen:** live Home Assistant startup/add-integration flow, most recently on the current mixed `0.1.86` install under `/config`
- **current observed behavior:** the historical backup-artifact import failures remain the reason this bug exists, but the stale state in this entry was overstating the current live blocker. In this watchdog run, the documented HA SSH fingerprint path reports `legacy_artifacts` empty, so the live install is not currently showing the earlier sibling-backup, nested `backup*`, or stale `backup*.pyc` pollution. The remaining blocker is exact-build drift on the six tracked component files under ZNE-022, not fresh evidence of active backup discovery pollution.
- **expected behavior:** selecting or loading Zero Net Export should import only the real `custom_components.zero_net_export` package, never any backup pseudo-module path.
- **evidence:** earlier live evidence on 2026-04-15 confirmed multiple `zero_net_export.backup_*` sibling directories under `/config/custom_components/`, and later HA logs showed the `backup_20260419_0009` import failure plus a lingering `custom_components/zero_net_export/__pycache__/backup.cpython-311.pyc` artifact. In this watchdog run, the documented HA SSH path still works (`root@192.168.86.200:2222`) and `python3 /root/.openclaw/workspace/projects/zero-net-export/scripts/validate_install_fingerprint.py /config --ssh-host root@192.168.86.200 --ssh-port 2222` now reports `legacy_artifacts` empty while still returning `overall_match=false` for the six tracked component mismatches. That means the earlier artifact-pollution evidence remains historically valid, but it is no longer the current live state.
- **suspected cause:** legacy cleanup and backup hardening covered sibling `zero_net_export.backup_*` paths under `/config/custom_components/`, plus nested `backup_*` children under the live package, but not a plain nested `backup.py` / `backup.cpython-*.pyc` variant inside `custom_components/zero_net_export`. Those artifacts can still be discovered as `custom_components.zero_net_export.backup` and break startup/config-flow import resolution.
- **repo fix:** the earlier repo fix already moved default deploy backups outside the Home Assistant discovery root and added cleanup for sibling `zero_net_export.backup_*` directories plus `zero_net_export.*.pyc` artifacts. A later fix widened `scripts/clean_legacy_discovery_artifacts.py` so it also detects and removes the plain nested `backup` module name alongside `backup_*`/`backup-*` children and matching `backup*.pyc` bytecode under `custom_components/zero_net_export/__pycache__`. Another follow-on closed the matching deploy leak in `scripts/deploy_exact_repo_build.py`: exact-build deploys now skip `__pycache__`, `.pyc`, and `.pyo` artifacts instead of copying ignored repo bytecode such as `__pycache__/backup.cpython-311.pyc` into Home Assistant. This run closes the remaining helper gap in the same path: `scripts/deploy_exact_repo_build.py` now actively removes legacy sibling backup directories, nested `backup*` children, and stale backup bytecode from the destination `custom_components` tree before it copies the fresh component and runs fingerprint validation. This run also keeps the validation blind spot closed: `scripts/compare_install_fingerprint.py` and `scripts/validate_install_fingerprint.py` surface `legacy_artifacts` explicitly and force `overall_match=false` while stale backup discovery artifacts are still present, so release/fingerprint checks can no longer look green against a polluted install path. `tests/test_install_helper_scripts.py` now locks both the deploy cleanup and comparison behavior in place.
- **validation status:** repo-side cleanup/deploy hardening was already implemented and verified with `python3 -m unittest tests.test_install_helper_scripts -q`. This watchdog run materially improves the live state for this bug class: the HA SSH fingerprint check now returns an empty `legacy_artifacts` section, so the previously documented sibling-backup, nested-backup, and stale-bytecode pollution is not currently present. Keep this bug at `fixed_pending_validation` until a future approved deploy/restart cycle confirms the import path stays clean in logs as well, but the current blocker has narrowed back to ZNE-022's mixed-build drift.
- **next action:** do not treat backup-artifact cleanup as the active blocker unless a new deploy/restart reintroduces import-pollution evidence. On the next approved live deploy, keep using the hardened exact-deploy path, but prioritize clearing ZNE-022's six-file drift and then confirm post-restart logs stay free of `custom_components.zero_net_export.backup*` import errors before closing this bug.

## ZNE-020 - Install provenance fingerprinting performs blocking file I/O in the event loop
- **status:** `fixed_pending_validation`
- **severity:** `medium`
- **area:** `runtime`
- **where seen:** live Home Assistant on the older installed `0.1.83` component build, plus earlier exact-build validation of commit `e1dcef8`
- **current observed behavior:** the repo fix exists, but the currently installed Home Assistant copy is still old enough to emit blocking `read_bytes` and `open` warnings from `release_info.py` while building install-provenance metadata from `manifest.json`
- **expected behavior:** install-provenance and release-info helpers should avoid synchronous filesystem reads on the event loop during coordinator/update paths
- **evidence:** documented HA SSH access on `root@192.168.86.200:2222` succeeded again in this run. `ha core logs -n 400 | grep -i zero_net_export` still shows `Detected blocking call to read_bytes ... at custom_components/zero_net_export/release_info.py, line 62: sha256_12 = hashlib.sha256(path.read_bytes()).hexdigest()[:12]` plus the matching blocking `open` warning at `2026-04-16 00:09:48`. The earlier exact-build validation against commit `e1dcef8` had cleared those warnings after restart, so this run's renewed warning is consistent with the current live fingerprint drift rather than a newly disproven repo fix.
- **suspected cause:** `build_install_provenance()` ultimately called `_cached_install_provenance()`, which still fell back to synchronous manifest/hash reads from `release_info.py` when the earlier warmup path had not produced a stable shared snapshot for later sync consumers on the event loop; the current live symptom persists because Home Assistant is still running an older `release_info.py` than repo HEAD
- **repo fix:** `e1dcef8` - replace the install-provenance warmup with an explicit async-primed snapshot in `custom_components/zero_net_export/release_info.py`, make synchronous callers fall back to a non-blocking pending snapshot instead of doing file I/O on the event loop, and refresh that snapshot during both setup-entry and migrate-entry startup in `custom_components/zero_net_export/__init__.py`; `tests/test_release_info_install_guidance.py` now covers the pending-snapshot fallback plus the new executor priming path
- **validation status:** repo-side fix remains verified with `python3 -m unittest tests.test_release_info_install_guidance -q`, `python3 -m unittest discover -s tests -q`, and `python3 -m py_compile custom_components/zero_net_export/release_info.py custom_components/zero_net_export/__init__.py`. Earlier live validation on the exact fixed build had also succeeded. However, this bug cannot stay `validated` as the current live state because the installed component fingerprint has drifted again and the old blocking-call warning is presently visible in Home Assistant logs.
- **next action:** treat exact-build redeploy as the immediate prerequisite under ZNE-022, then rerun post-restart log review and close this only after the current installed build no longer emits the blocking `release_info.py` warnings

## ZNE-045 - Fingerprint payload still let `expected_commit` drift with repo-head bookkeeping
- **status:** `fixed_pending_validation`
- **severity:** `medium`
- **area:** `release`
- **where seen:** repo-side fingerprint-helper audit on 2026-04-18, with live HA SSH validation recheck in the same run
- **current observed behavior:** `docs/VALIDATION_CHECKLIST.md`, `README.md`, and the earlier ZNE-043 closure all said fingerprint guidance had been corrected so deploy decisions could stay anchored on the component-changing build, but the helper payload itself still emitted `expected_commit` as full repo HEAD whenever `scripts/compare_install_fingerprint.py` built its own expected payload. In practice that meant doc-only or test-only commits could still move one of the primary comparison fields and reintroduce the same false release-candidate churn the supervisor explicitly warns against.
- **expected behavior:** the emitted comparison payload should keep `expected_commit`, `expected_component_commit`, and `preferred_validation_commit` aligned on the latest component-changing commit, while exposing full repo HEAD separately as `repo_head_commit`, so helper output, docs, and bug-tracker guidance all describe the same deploy anchor.
- **evidence:** repo inspection in this run confirmed `scripts/print_expected_install_fingerprint.py` and the no-`--expected-json` path in `scripts/compare_install_fingerprint.py` were still setting `expected_commit` from `git rev-parse --short HEAD` even though the surrounding guidance already told operators to treat component commit as the real shipped-build anchor. The documented HA SSH path in `TOOLS.md` also worked again in this run: `python3 scripts/validate_install_fingerprint.py /config/custom_components --ssh-host root@192.168.86.200 --ssh-port 2222` still reports the same unchanged 10-file live mismatch set, and the refreshed expected payload now renders `expected_commit=ad84902`, `expected_component_commit=ad84902`, `preferred_validation_commit=ad84902`, and `repo_head_commit=be623a4`, which matches the intended component-anchor semantics instead of rotating with doc-only repo HEAD.
- **suspected cause:** the earlier fingerprint-guidance cleanup updated deploy wording and added `preferred_validation_commit`, but left the legacy `expected_commit` field bound to repo HEAD in the helper payload and compare fallback path.
- **repo fix:** this run's fingerprint-anchor follow-up commit - update `scripts/print_expected_install_fingerprint.py` and the repo-head fallback in `scripts/compare_install_fingerprint.py` so `expected_commit` is the component-changing validation anchor, add `repo_head_commit` as the separate full-repo marker, refresh `tests/test_install_helper_scripts.py`, and align `README.md` plus `docs/VALIDATION_CHECKLIST.md` with the corrected payload contract.
- **validation status:** repo-side fix implemented and remains valid. Verification passed with the documented HA SSH validation path above plus `python3 -m unittest tests.test_install_helper_scripts -q`, and the payload still keeps `expected_commit`, `expected_component_commit`, and `preferred_validation_commit` aligned on the component-changing build instead of doc-only repo HEAD. A later watchdog run reopened ZNE-022 after a fresh HA SSH fingerprint recheck returned `overall_match=false` again, so this helper fix should be treated as still valid repo-side while the live install once again requires explicit deploy/restart approval before exact-build validation can be considered green.
- **next action:** keep the watchdog focused on remaining `0.1.87` implementation work or an explicitly approved deploy, not another fingerprint-anchor wording refresh.

## ZNE-058 - Promotion picker labels still leaked live state into shortlist-style candidate previews
- **status:** `fixed_pending_validation`
- **severity:** `medium`
- **area:** `managed_devices`
- **where seen:** repo audit on 2026-04-20 while comparing `custom_components/zero_net_export/config_flow.py` against `docs/UI_DESIGN.md` and `docs/UI_IMPLEMENTATION_MAP.md`
- **current observed behavior:** the managed-device promotion picker had already dropped the older `state on` / `state off` leak, but the same shortlist/full-list labels still felt too helper-ish in two ways: mixed-backlog rows duplicated `review first` in strings like `Suggested now, review first: ... | review first | key warning: ...`, and even the cleaned top row still over-ranked one choice as `Suggested now` instead of using the more neutral surfaced-candidate posture the design calls for. This run found the same ranking drift still leaking through the surrounding form copy in `strings.json` and `translations/en.json`, where the shortlist intro still said `best surfaced unmanaged ...` and called itself a `short, opinionated promotion shortlist`, which contradicted the design rule to keep unmanaged surfacing neutral instead of pretending the product already knows the one correct next choice.
- **expected behavior:** promotion picker labels should match the same shortlist-style unmanaged preview used elsewhere in Managed Devices, without lower-value live-state fragments diluting the review-first or ready-next story.
- **evidence:** an earlier repo inspection found `_device_candidates()` in `custom_components/zero_net_export/config_flow.py` still calling `build_candidate_preview(..., include_state=True)` for the label reused by `_candidate_options()`, and that original state leak is already fixed. This run's follow-on repo audit found `_candidate_picker_label(...)` still prefixing review-first labels with `Review first` or `Suggested now, review first` while leaving the same `| review first |` fragment inside the candidate preview itself, and still calling the first surfaced option `Suggested now` even after the state leak was removed. `docs/UI_DESIGN.md` explicitly says each unmanaged candidate should show a concise shortlist-style preview with name, type, likely usefulness, and key warning, and that the unmanaged section should stay useful but neutral in posture rather than over-ranking one supposedly correct next choice. `docs/UI_IMPLEMENTATION_MAP.md` likewise says Workstream C should remove remaining raw-id, helper-ish, or ambiguous wording from the promotion flow.
- **suspected cause:** earlier Workstream C cleanup fixed the promotion shortlist recap and device-page review copy, but the picker-label helper itself was still carrying the older state-heavy candidate preview.
- **repo fix:** the earlier fix updated `custom_components/zero_net_export/config_flow.py` so discovered candidate labels call `build_candidate_preview(..., include_state=False)` and added a focused regression in `tests/test_config_flow_device_runtime_overlay.py` to lock the picker preview on shortlist-style copy without `state ...` drift. The prior follow-on then closed the mixed-backlog duplication leak by stripping the duplicated `| review first |` fragment whenever the picker prefix already said `Review first` or `Suggested now, review first`. A later run replaced `Suggested now` with `Top surfaced` / `Top surfaced, review first` and aligned the surrounding shortlist/full-list copy in `custom_components/zero_net_export/strings.json` and `custom_components/zero_net_export/translations/en.json` so the shortlist stayed neutral instead of sounding opinionated. This run closes the remaining ranking drift left behind by that follow-on: `_candidate_picker_label(...)`, the shared Managed Devices strings/translations, and the device-page review notifications now use `Currently surfaced` / `Currently surfaced, review first` / `Currently surfaced unmanaged candidate(s)` instead of `Top surfaced ...`, so the native fleet review stops sounding like it already knows the single best next device while preserving the review-first and ready-next backlog cues. `tests/test_config_flow_device_runtime_overlay.py`, `tests/test_bucket_ownership_copy.py`, and `tests/test_button_entity_categories.py` now lock that wording in place.
- **validation status:** repo-side fix verified in this run with `python3 -m unittest -q tests.test_config_flow_device_runtime_overlay tests.test_bucket_ownership_copy tests.test_button_entity_categories` plus `python3 -m py_compile custom_components/zero_net_export/config_flow.py custom_components/zero_net_export/button.py`, which keeps the picker labels, shared strings, and device-page review copy aligned on the more neutral `Currently surfaced` wording. Live Home Assistant validation is still pending on the next exact-build deploy.
- **next action:** include this wording cleanup in the next exact-build deploy, then confirm the live shortlist/full-list selectors and device-page review surfaces keep the stronger shortlist-style preview without the leftover `Top surfaced` ranking language in Home Assistant.
